  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_a90e1845-dd43-4c51-bacc-429cb8bac29a'
      });
    }

And the deeper Sophie searches, the farther the conspiracy stretches, proving that her most dangerous enemy might be closer than she realizes.<br /><br />In this nail-biting third book in the Keeper of the Lost Cities series, Sophie must fight the flames of rebellion, before they destroy everyone and everything she loves.</span>

  <span id="freeText11192254272195291157" style="display:none">Since we all know I'm a fan of my own books, I thought I'd use this space to answer a few of questions I keep hearing:<br /><br />- Yes--this book AWESOME.     <a title="Lucy Tonks" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/90494494-lucy-tonks"><img alt="Lucy Tonks" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1593371745p2/90494494.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2624449056?book_show_action=true">Nov 11, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lucy Tonks" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lucy Tonks" href="/user/show/90494494-lucy-tonks">Lucy Tonks</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2624449056" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11717030868399868227"><i>"She wasn't going to cry. She was going to fight."</i><br/><br/>I loved this book and I'll probably say the same thing for every book in the series, but I just love this story so much. The characters are amazing, the plot is so good and let's know forget how beautiful the covers are. Honestly, these books deserve more recognition than they are actually getting. <br/><br/>I love the cast of characters so much. Everyone brings something to the story, no exceptions. Keefe is and will forever be my favourite character in t</span>
  <span id="freeText11717030868399868227" style="display:none"><i>"She wasn't going to cry. She was going to fight."</i><br /><br />I loved this book and I'll probably say the same thing for every book in the series, but I just love this story so much. The characters are amazing, the plot is so good and let's know forget how beautiful the covers are. Honestly, these books deserve more recognition than they are actually getting. <br /><br />I love the cast of characters so much. Everyone brings something to the story, no exceptions. Keefe is and will forever be my favourite character in the series. His sass is all I need and with it he brings a lighter tone to the story. By the way, Team Foster-Keefe is superior! <br /><br />The friendship between Dex and Sophie is one of my favourites in this series. Although, both of them screw things up, a lot, they are always there for eachother and god I really want to have a friendship as theirs. <br /><br />The plot was amazing, I never got bored. I was hooked from page one. I loved all the plots and twists and by the end of the book my heart was slowly breaking for Keefe. He is so precious, he shouldn't have to go through this. I actually am pround of myself for figuring out something that happened at the ned of the book, like the clues we are there. <br /><br />I beg you, if you have not read this book do it. Trust me, it is worth it. There will be times when you would laugh (like a lot), there will be times when you'd feel your heart breaking, but so far the rollercoaster of emotions was worth it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11717030868399868227" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2956920155" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2956920155" />
    <a title="BrooKe" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/87485390-brooke"><img alt="BrooKe" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1583732525p2/87485390.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2956920155?book_show_action=true">Sep 24, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="BrooKe" class="user" itemprop="url" name="BrooKe" href="/user/show/87485390-brooke">BrooKe</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2956920155" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9278401113746804725">4.7/5 | Five stars for the cover alone.<br/><br/>This cover. Is fucking <i>gorgeous</i>. It may just be my favourite of the series, perhaps my favourite in the history of book covers I’ve ever encountered. It captures such an impactful moment so immaculately in terms of meaning and beauty. The colour scheme is gorgeous, really selling the whole magical, ethereal quality of the Lost Cities—not to mention it’s somehow accentuated by the title of the book: <b>Everblaze</b>. Of course it also helps that a fetching Fitz and</span>
  <span id="freeText9278401113746804725" style="display:none">4.7/5 | Five stars for the cover alone.<br /><br />This cover. Is fucking <i>gorgeous</i>. It may just be my favourite of the series, perhaps my favourite in the history of book covers I’ve ever encountered. It captures such an impactful moment so immaculately in terms of meaning and beauty. The colour scheme is gorgeous, really selling the whole magical, ethereal quality of the Lost Cities—not to mention it’s somehow accentuated by the title of the book: <b>Everblaze</b>. Of course it also helps that a fetching Fitz and Sophie illustration takes centre stage (GAH I love them so much!)<br /><br /><br /><b>P L O T</b><br /><br /><b>So we opened with Keefe and that was when I knew it was going to be a good book.</b><br /><br />Okay, fine, I’m joking. Mostly. <br /><br />In all seriousness, the beginning was incredible for reasons other than Keefe (though let us not forget he is always a generous contribute to my happiness). There was exploration of wondrous and, might I add, <i>illegal</i> places, mind-bending riddle solving and, at the centre of it all, the best character dynamic by far in this series: Sophie and Keefe.<br /><br />Compare that to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13260670.Exile__Keeper_of_the_Lost_Cities___2_" title="Exile (Keeper of the Lost Cities, #2) by Shannon Messenger" rel="nofollow noopener">Exile</a> where we spent like 300 pages on Sophie trying to get a completely random, annoying as hell alicorn to trust her! The difference in these openings marked the difference in plot to come because, from the very beginning of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13260668.Everblaze__Keeper_of_the_Lost_Cities___3_" title="Everblaze (Keeper of the Lost Cities, #3) by Shannon Messenger" rel="nofollow noopener">Everblaze</a>, the events were much more ominous and <i>plenty</i> more enticing.<br /><br />There was so much action that made this book addicting, as well. For example, the event illustrated in the eye-wateringly magnificent cover almost had me tearing up in real life! There was also the scene at the Wandering Woods, the Grady being a flawed fucking <b>badass</b> scene, the Councillors’ chosen punishment, the battle on the mountain. Oh the DRAMA! So much of it. So many emotions, so much heartbreak, so much romantic, familial and platonic love.<br /><br />And <b>THE PACING</b>! Oh the bloody pacing! It’s the best thing ever. There was a rampage of action sequences that had my heart racing but it was never overwhelming because, dispersed between said sequences, was witty and meaningful dialogue mixed with banter and other clever and casual means of characterisation.<br /><br />I didn’t mention this in the last two books but I always thought the concept of the Wandering Woods was so poetic! Instead of burying corpses, the elves plant personalised trees to represent the deceased, signifying that a part of you will always live on or maybe even conveying how premature their deaths were since elves have such a long lifespan. This is a brilliant example of how it should be <i>SHOWN</i> how the elvin world is better than the human world in this series rather than just being <i>told</i> 47 times like in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12842828.Keeper_of_the_Lost_Cities__Keeper_of_the_Lost_Cities___1_" title="Keeper of the Lost Cities (Keeper of the Lost Cities, #1) by Shannon Messenger" rel="nofollow noopener">Keeper of the Lost Cities</a> how superior they are.<br /><br />To bring this gush to a close, I really liked that the rebels are painted as the bad guys as opposed to some wronged organisation rebelling against the immoral higher ups for a ‘just’ cause. It isn’t like <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2767052.The_Hunger_Games__The_Hunger_Games___1_" title="The Hunger Games (The Hunger Games, #1) by Suzanne Collins" rel="nofollow noopener">The Hunger Games</a> or <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/27774758.An_Ember_in_the_Ashes__An_Ember_in_the_Ashes___1_" title="An Ember in the Ashes (An Ember in the Ashes, #1) by Sabaa Tahir" rel="nofollow noopener">An Ember in the Ashes</a> from the rebel heroes’ perspective but rather the government is dealing with the transgressive, violent rebels. It also shows disagreements between said higher ups so that there may be those 'in the right' and those 'in the wrong'; a whole range of different vantage points is explored. It’s refreshing because the honourable, ethical rebels is something I’ve read many, many times (granted, usually well done) and a change was very much welcome.<br /><br /><br /><b>C H A R A C T E R S</b><br /><br />I usually go through this section character by character but let me just first and foremost establish that my absolute favourite part of this book had to be, hands down, <b>the Keefe drama</b>. I can’t go into it because spoilers but this sunshine kid, who we learnt last book becomes a shadow at home, had to deal with so many life-altering revelations and he and others surrounding him acted accordingly. The execution was phenomenal. Not only did it give a character I care for so deeply millions of layers of added depth but it also meant that the plot didn’t revolve around Sophie! I think <i>THAT</i> was the game changer that boosted <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13260668.Everblaze__Keeper_of_the_Lost_Cities___3_" title="Everblaze (Keeper of the Lost Cities, #3) by Shannon Messenger" rel="nofollow noopener">Everblaze</a> from a 4 star read to a 5 star read! If you think about it, my List Of Things Sophie Gets That No One Else Does Because She’s Special was significantly shorter this time around! It gave other characters a chance to shine.<br /><br />Sophie Foster is a smart, compassionate girl and I really like her. She is largely in the spotlight of every installment—everything is about her—and this definitely grew old fast. While this was mostly the case in Everblaze as well, other characters got a chance and I think this served to not only help <i>them</i> grow as characters but it also benefited Sophie. I really just want to see what she’d be like in a supporting role! This may be the closest I’ll ever get to that so I’ll take what I can get. <br /><br />Here is my significantly shorter List of Things Sophie Gets That No One Else Does Because She’s Special: <br />Sophie can breach ogre minds when no one else ever could, Sophie can implant memories, Sophie still has 37748291028372 powers (for most of the book, anyway), Sophie has the power to almost wage a war because everyone cares <i>that much</i> about what a thirteen-year-old thinks, Sophie is literally called the star prodigy of all of Foxfire in front of other students by the principal. Isn’t it Principal 101 that favouritism is frowned upon?<br /><br />Sophie handles a ridiculous amount of bullshit yet again. I still have yet to understand why everything is her and only <b>HER</b> burden to bear when sometimes it legitimately isn’t. At least I can say this irritating factor was dialled down a little the third time writing a Keeper review. Despite Sophie’s lack of imperfections, I still really do like her and enjoy her as a protagonist—especially in excruciatingly relatable moments like this:<br /><br /><i>“Sophie thought slowly, fairly certain her brain was about to call it quits.”</i><br /><br />Keefe, my love, my driving force. Is it just me or are his jokes becoming even MORE forced? In any other case, this would annoy me immensely, but, in this case, I applaud thee, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/5265998.Shannon_Messenger" title="Shannon Messenger" rel="nofollow noopener">Shannon Messenger</a>. As his life continues to crumble, his jokes become more inappropriate and less humourous. I adore this type of character as they truly make my heart break the most because of how strong they are, covering up their misery with jokes for the benefit of others or perhaps even because they don’t know how to handle grief (as Keefe admitted in Exile). The execution was largely successful seeing as I still adore Keefe overall but sometimes it was a little problematic—especially towards the beginning of the book. <br /><br />See, his transitions between incessant jokester and abused child were kind of... jerky? I’m all for these deeper levels of his but I just wish his personas were handled more carefully. It’s difficult to explain. It’s just that one moment he’d be on about sparkly poo and then the next he’d have his eyes trained on the ground, refusing to look at anyone. The switch from one to the other is a little too drastic for my taste. Too unrealistic—forced, even. But, hey, I’m nitpicking and this issue vanished quicker than Biana around the two-third mark of the book. Keefe’s the kind of guy that hides his negative emotions behind a smile, masking fear as a joke. I’ve said it before and I’ll say it again: <b>I love that character concept</b>. And don’t get me wrong: Keefe isn’t merely a concept but rather a <b>remarkably well-rounded character</b>.<br /><br /><i>“I want you to know that I’m not going to sit at home anymore, worrying about what might happen to you, or Keefe, or Biana, or my dad. I’m going to be right there with you guys, helping any way I can.”</i><br /><br />I’ve also said <i>this</i> before and I’ll say it again: Fitz is FIERCE and very passionate. He did kind of become more of the ‘nice guy’ he was in Keeper rather than the fireball in Exile which was mildly disappointing but, hey, you can’t have it all! He’s supportive and smart and all but lacks flare. He’s definitely growing on me and, technically speaking, I really like him, but what I want is to LOVE him like I do Keefe or at least to like him as much as I like Sophie. For that to happen, I need him to be more of a fireball like last book (but less of an asshole than he was in the last book, mind you) or possess some discerning characteristic other than ‘Wonderboy’. ‘Wonderboy’ is <b>not</b> a flaw! <b>Being too perfect is not a flaw!</b> Well, okay, it is, but not the kind that makes me like someone!<br /><br />Biana who? Is Biana even a main character? I’m sure she’s supposed to be yet she gets a fifth of the time Fitz or Keefe get in the front and centre. She’s meant to be Sophie’s age but then why do I feel like she’s so much younger than her—like she’s nine or something? She likes fashion, she has a crush on Keefe, she’s beautiful and powerful. That’s it. Girl needs some growth! All I can say (and this isn’t even strictly about Biana) is that I’m glad we’re not going down the cliche route of her living in her older brother’s shadow. I much prefer that the whole Vacker family are early bloomers as opposed to the ‘ugly duckling’ trope.<br /><br />I firmly believe everyone was WAY too hard on Dex. Sure, he fucked up, but did he know he would? NO! He’s a thirteen-year-old boy, for god’s sake! His reasons were totally understandable and he didn’t even know what he was getting into. All he wanted was to make his family, who adores him and is constantly unjustly slandered, proud! UGH.<br /><br />And just <i>what</i> is Marella's problemo?<br /><br />Alden, AKA ‘No reason to worry’, was kind of brief but it’s all made up for because of that hilarious code Sophie, Fitz, Keefe and Biana devised. Grady is a king and nobody can convince me otherwise. Edaline is... slightly more interesting than she was before but is still almost as bland as cardboard, to be honest.<br /><br />I <i>KNEW</i> I’d wind up liking Bronte! From the moment this asshole showed his pointy ears, I was certain he’d be among the most complex characters in the cast. His hatred for Sophie always seemed superficial to me because it was so overdone! I guessed he’d be a Severus Snape but done better, and so far so good.<br /><br /><br /><b>R E L A T I O N S H I P S</b><br /><br />Where, oh where, do I begin?<br /><br />Let’s start collectively: the main friendship group. <br /><br /><i>“She turned to study the faces of her friends—the faces that had been with her through everything. She’d fought so hard to protect them that she hadn’t really considered how much they protected her.”</i><br /><br />But here’s the catch: I’m talking about each character’s friendship with Sophie alone. Amongst themselves, Fitz, Keefe, Dex and Biana barely interact. For instance, it has long been established that Keefe and Fitz are best friends... but where’s the <b>evidence</b>? Other than Keefe being over at Everglen a lot, there isn’t any indication. It’s all talk and no tell and I could really use more of this friendship. Same goes for Biana and Fitz like these two are meant to be siblings yet I have zero grasp of their dynamic other than perhaps them flaunting their abilities to one another and being equally annoying about it. And Dex is <i>such</i> an outcast in this group; he hates Fitz and Biana and only tolerates Keefe. I’m afraid he’ll be conveniently ‘left behind’ because he just doesn’t fit! I suppose it’s difficult to accomplish all the relations when this is all following Sophie but I still think more could be done. <br /><br />Oh yeah and what is this crush Biana has on Keefe that gets approximately one sentence of mention per book? <b>That sentence count better increase.</b><br /><br />Romance takes a backseat which did not quell my Sophie-Keefe shipping... but still! I don’t know if there is anything I like more than a book with subtle, if any, romance that still makes my heart ache for it! It’s the perfect recipe for an angsty but sweet slow-burn romance.<br /><br />Keefe and Sophie are proper confidants, being the first to team up every time. It's almost by default now. The only thing I like about freaking Silveny is that she helped bring these two together. Their relationship has obviously progressed with all the casual handholding and, dare I say, simply holding each other? JUST SAYING! But most of all, I adore how Sophie is the only one <b>truly</b> there for Keefe with all he goes through. Honestly, if these two don’t get together, I will <b>definitely</b> throw a giant fit, but as long as their friendship remains this pure, if they don’t get together I’ll perhaps let it slide and binge fanfiction of them as opposed to hating this series for wronging me so. <br /><br /><i>“Breathe, Foster,” Keefe whispered, giving her palm a quick, reassuring squeeze.<br />She clung to his hand like it could keep her alive and forced herself to take a shaky breath.”</i><br /><br />I’ve decided I’m fine with Fitz and Sophie. He cares a lot for her and is almost desperate to help her in any way he can. My issue is that it reminds me a little bit too much of how Alden cares for her; as if she’s his responsibility. It’s always so serious with them whilst, let’s say, with Keefe it’s always a lot more fun and for leisure rather than duty. She even seems to have more fun around freaking <i>Dex</i> than Fitz. Sophie just doesn’t seem super at ease with him because the tension is always so high. Also, the reason for their closeness is because Tiergen was basically playing matchmaker with Sophie and Fitz ‘for plot reasons’ because they <i>needed</i> to trust each other... you know, for the good of the world.<br /><br />I mean, to their credit, Fitz and Sophie made me <b>aw</b> more than once. Even if they are being kind of forced to trust one another for plot reasons, the process of doing so is resulting in cute moments that are making me slightly conflicted. <br /><br />I do like this ship. It’s cute so far, but it’s just that <b>Keefe and Sophie are better</b>.<br /><br />What else? Sophie, Grady and Edaline made me cry once more because they’re so sweet. I repeat the same thing in every Keeper review because <b>SERIOUSLY I CANNOT FOR THE LIFE OF ME GET OVER HOW SWEET THEY ARE.</b><br /><br />I’m ending on the same note I did last time: Keefe’s family. It’s just so INTERESTING. He wilts in their presence, he isn’t himself around them because they disapprove of who he is and, well, let us not forget the things he learns about them!<br /><br />... ...<br /><br />I am binging this series and my grades are suffering for it but I almost don’t care.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9278401113746804725" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2595295046" />
    <a title="Faith M:)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/72681153-faith-m"><img alt="Faith M:)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1534517329p2/72681153.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2595295046?book_show_action=true">Dec 14, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Faith M:)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Faith M:)" href="/user/show/72681153-faith-m">Faith M:)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/72681153-faith-m?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/72681153-faith-m?shelf=adventure-fantasy">adventure-fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2595295046" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9010618267073944995">I LOVEEE THIS SERIES!!!!! This has quickly become my favorite book series EVER!!! <br/><br/>Here are the stats: <br/><br/>Romance- Clean! Crushes- but that’s it:) <br/><br/>Violence / Content- Definitely some in this area. Several fight scenes, near-death experiences, betrayals of close friends, death of a main character, etc. <br/><br/>*Cautious readers beware: One fight scene is more descriptive than others. Two people are very angry in a fight. One character burns the others hand off. They are both trying to kill each other. Neithe</span>
  <span id="freeText9010618267073944995" style="display:none">I LOVEEE THIS SERIES!!!!! This has quickly become my favorite book series EVER!!! <br /><br />Here are the stats: <br /><br />Romance- Clean! Crushes- but that’s it:) <br /><br />Violence / Content- Definitely some in this area. Several fight scenes, near-death experiences, betrayals of close friends, death of a main character, etc. <br /><br />*Cautious readers beware: One fight scene is more descriptive than others. Two people are very angry in a fight. One character burns the others hand off. They are both trying to kill each other. Neither dies, but this is a more descriptive fight scene.* <br /><br />*squeals* I LOVE THIS SERIES❤️ Never in a book series have I been so attached to the characters! The writing style is intriguing, the characters are so lovable, the friendships are goals... <br /><br />In the first book, I was team Sophitz ALL THE WAY. Second book, Keefe started to grow on me. Now- I am so confused. I love both Fitz and Keefe so much! But maybe Fitz a little more... ;) <br /><br />And Dex... I love him:) He is so kind and supportive to Sophie. I loved seeing him use his ability- even if it gets him in trouble sometimes... <br /><br />Bianna was in this book a lot! I loved seeing her manifest an ability! <br /><br />And of course... Grady and Edaline❤️ They’re such good parents... <br /><br />I cannot wait to read the rest of this series! Will reread these over and over again.<br /><br />I think I'm still #Team Fitz...</span>
  <a data-text-id="9010618267073944995" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2073956074" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2073956074" />
    <a title="Maddie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/60336580-maddie"><img alt="Maddie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1498658110p2/60336580.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2073956074?book_show_action=true">Jul 29, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Maddie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Maddie" href="/user/show/60336580-maddie">Maddie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2073956074" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5475728335598637050">3?<br/><br/>I know I’m not this series’s target demographic. But I still think this series has issues that would have bothered me even when I <i>was</i> in the target demo. Specifically: (1) the characters not spending a ton of time at Foxfire, (2) the characters/factions not having motivations that make sense and several of the characters changing drastically between books without much explanation, (3) the way science is used, and (4) the number of characters and their development (or lack thereof). I also don'</span>
  <span id="freeText5475728335598637050" style="display:none">3?<br /><br />I know I’m not this series’s target demographic. But I still think this series has issues that would have bothered me even when I <i>was</i> in the target demo. Specifically: (1) the characters not spending a ton of time at Foxfire, (2) the characters/factions not having motivations that make sense and several of the characters changing drastically between books without much explanation, (3) the way science is used, and (4) the number of characters and their development (or lack thereof). I also don't think I've ever been this enraged about a love triangle/square in a long while. <br /><br />This book is the only book in the series that comes even close to having an actual plot that makes sense. While I thought the second book was fun and a big step up from the the first, it was really bogged down by the way "science" was used to hand-wave a lot of the things about Sophie/her backstory that don't make sense. Which is a problem, because these books have what is essentially magic, and you don't NEED science in a world that has magic. Science has to follow strict rules and can't violate the laws of nature. Magic, but definition, violates the laws of nature. <br /><br />These books have a serious case of Plot Convenience that makes it difficult for me to take them seriously. They borrow a lot from Harry Potter, Charlie Bone, Percy Jackson and other similar series, and yet fail to grasp why those books work. Namely because there are well-defined 'rules' and limits regarding magic/special powers and the characters are continually put in situations that they have to get creative to wiggle their way out of, generally by using their combined strengths. All three series of the above mentioned series also have strong world building and make the motivations of the villains explicit from the get-go. <br /><br />Because the world in this series doesn't make a lot of sense, and because neither the motivations of the bad or good guys make sense or are even explained, none of the characters really have motivations that are well-defined or make sense. A lot of them have kind of surface level motivations (Alden being a good example), but there are very few characters in this series who feel like complete, complex characters. I think Sandor and Keefe are really the only two, with Sophie, Dex, Grady and Edaline on the cusp. <br /><br />Overall: I think this series is fun, has potential, and does a few things very well (the adult characters and the subtle, nuanced way grief is handled). They're also fast-paced and good pallet cleansers for denser reads. But there is a lot that is missing that I think it inexcusable at this point in the series and I don't have much hope Messenger will be able to turn it around.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5475728335598637050" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer17022572664825767203">Initially, I was going to give this a 2-star rating, but after reading the last few chapters, I decided to increase it to three.<br/><br/>This book was a bit dreary compared to the first two books, and has the same formula. Sophie is so talented that she gets into trouble, and then cue her friends (either one or all of them) or the Black Swan to save her then she saved them after and the end - back to Havenfield (or Everglen) for recovery. Then repeat the cycle all over again.<br/><br/>I didn't like Sophie much in </span>
  <span id="freeText17022572664825767203" style="display:none">Initially, I was going to give this a 2-star rating, but after reading the last few chapters, I decided to increase it to three.<br /><br />This book was a bit dreary compared to the first two books, and has the same formula. Sophie is so talented that she gets into trouble, and then cue her friends (either one or all of them) or the Black Swan to save her then she saved them after and the end - back to Havenfield (or Everglen) for recovery. Then repeat the cycle all over again.<br /><br />I didn't like Sophie much in this book. She is selfish and doesn't think of the consequences of her actions. Then after everything goes wrong, she will feel sorry for herself <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[because is so talented and why can't she be normal - and how can she be normal if she keeps chasing the dangers herself? <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> Good thing her adiptive parents are the most forgiving person in their world, or else she will be in so much trouble.<br /><br />The redeeming quality in this book are her friends. Good thing that they can think and act for themselves even without the help of Sophie. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ And Keefe. My dear Keefe. He had been through a lot in this book and he needs a hug. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />I don't know if I'm going to continue reading the series now or will wait for the last book to be published. Because I don't think that I will continue reading it if the next book is still the same as this.</span>

<div id="review_1087691505" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1087691505" />
    <a title="Ashley" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10901115-ashley"><img alt="Ashley" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1087691505?book_show_action=true">Oct 23, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ashley" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ashley" href="/user/show/10901115-ashley">Ashley</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10901115-ashley?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1087691505" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2869507911469116405">All I can say is...wow. This book took me on a huge roller-coaster ride that I wasn't prepared for at all, and wasn't expecting. Really, at all. I don't even know where to begin.<br/> <img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1424399026ra/13756953.gif' width='' height='' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/> <br/>So I wasn't planning on kinda wasting my day through the continual reading of this, but I did. Aaaand soooo. Let the review begin.<br/><br/>I have to admit, there was a lot of character development in this book. And the whole square (not triangle) kinda romance was in the background, but not prominent like I would have liked it </span>
  <span id="freeText2869507911469116405" style="display:none">All I can say is...wow. This book took me on a huge roller-coaster ride that I wasn't prepared for at all, and wasn't expecting. Really, at all. I don't even know where to begin.<br> <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1424399026ra/13756953.gif" width="" height="" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br>So I wasn't planning on kinda wasting my day through the continual reading of this, but I did. Aaaand soooo. Let the review begin.<br><br>I have to admit, there was a lot of character development in this book. And the whole square (not triangle) kinda romance was in the background, but not prominent like I would have liked it to be. And along the lines of that...<br>I am sooooo Team Keefe!!! Haha, he's awesome, and I love him :3. But I <i>did</i> find myself softening a lot towards Fitz, which is kinda crazy since I was totally not rooting for him at all when it came to Sophie's heart (Ugh, hate how a thirteen-year-old is actually having actual romance type of things, whereas I...don't *kinda rolls eyes*), but I definitely like him more now. And at first I was really afraid about the whole <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Dex possibly being Sophie's cousin thing <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>, which was a bit surprising since I wasn't exactly wanting him to be with her...but lol, glad that was all cleared up! <br>Okay uhm...well I really disliked at first, how there was so much you don't know, but once I hit the halfway point, things got craaaaaazy. And all this stuff was revealed that I just barely managed to predict a few sentences before happening, but mostly I had no idea what I was in for.<br>That's for sure. <br><br>There were moments where my eyes welled up <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[KENRIC. Uuuuuggghhh whyyyy did he have to diiiie?! That was the one big ship that I was DYING to see happen! I mean, with him and Oralie...and oh my gosh, I can't believe they couldn't be together because they were on the council and *draws in deep breath, fanning self a little* Okay...sorry. Just...THE FEELS <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> and I actually <i>cried</i> when <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[DEX, sobbing as he was basically forced to TORTURE Sophie. Somewhere during that whole scene I starting exclaiming about the council being totally EVIL and 'UUGH I HATE THIS!" XD  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> But gosh, the boy sure is loyal! And kinda awesome... *sigh* But sorry, I'm not going to be swayed over to his side/team. It's between Keefe and Fitz for me now....but actually really, I'm still totally...<br>TEAM KEEFE!!!<br><br>So I was gasping, yelling stuff, and opening my eyes wide with surprise/horror at various times throughout the book (ah, the joys of reading a book at home where no one can judge you). So I guess you can say overall I really liked the thing.<br>Which is really surprising, considering I only liked the other books...<br>And oh yes, I also cried happy tears at the whole <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Sophie finally calling Grady and Edaline 'Dad and mom' <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>.<br><br>Also, there were moments when I was super terrified, and said so out loud. <br>You'd think a middle grade book wouldn't leave me feel so drained and tired after reading it, but...yeah, it did.<br>Wonder if that happens to other readers ever...<br>So, bottom line is I really liked it, but I didn't love it.<br>Mainly because I don't think this is exactly my type of book per-say.<br>And yet I was sucked into it <i>so</i> easily, and I could barely look at any shortcomings or whatever else the thing might have because I was so IN the story.<br>Aaaand...that's it.<br><br>...<br>Think I'll eventually read the next book, when it comes out...</["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

<div id="review_2067983936" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2067983936" />
    <a title="Lauren" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/69681823-lauren"><img alt="Lauren" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2067983936?book_show_action=true">Jul 21, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lauren" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lauren" href="/user/show/69681823-lauren">Lauren</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer2067983936&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2067983936" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15658191215036345242">This series started with a lot of promise. An outcast telepathic girl thrown into a world she's never heard of, separate from humans, living with those of her species. Alright. Secrets surrounding a mysterious background, a shady covert organization with inexplicable ties to the protagonist's history. Cool! Superpowers for everyone, a society built up to be fair, no one considered poor or destitute. Sounds perfect! Except for the Talentless. Wait, what?<br/><br/>This world is perfect on the surface, but t</span>
  <span id="freeText15658191215036345242" style="display:none">This series started with a lot of promise. An outcast telepathic girl thrown into a world she's never heard of, separate from humans, living with those of her species. Alright. Secrets surrounding a mysterious background, a shady covert organization with inexplicable ties to the protagonist's history. Cool! Superpowers for everyone, a society built up to be fair, no one considered poor or destitute. Sounds perfect! Except for the Talentless. Wait, what?<br /><br />This world is perfect on the surface, but the closer one looks, the more glaring issues and concerns one finds. No one's discriminated against by skin color, sex, or birth status -- just by what they may or may not be able to do (control fire or no talent at all) with powers they're not supposed to use. No one's judged harshly or unfairly -- until the Council goes corrupt and can't be stopped. No one lives in an ugly place: everyone's surrounded by perfect grass and sky, untainted by pollution and modern technology. Rare gems are used to decorate everything from houses to clothes to jewelry. Can I get a Syndrome gif? "When everything's beautiful -- nothing is"? They couldn't care less about the morals or behavior of society, trusting instead to personal moral compasses that can be twisted at will.<br /><br />I have more issues with their world, but I think I'll move on. To Sophie.<br /><br />She started as a curious, accident-prone girl living in a new world without any familiar faces. Now, she's a passive, accident-prone teenager too afraid to consider her friends and family wrong that she won't do what her conscience thinks she should do. Landing in the hospital after every adventure was entertaining until this book. Then it was annoying and predictable.<br /><br />Sophie has some of the best talents, which is annoying in and of itself, but she doesn't ever really use them. The final conclusion of every book involves running away or watching as someone else confronts their enemies. Then someone has to console poor Sophie because she learned something new. This isn't just an ending issue: every time there's building conflict and action, there's an outlet and an anti-climactic conclusion. She runs into members of the enemy organization, and she prepares to attack, but then ends up listening to them talk about nothing. Then she returns to those she trusts, and all is well!<br /><br />I'd complain about the love-polyhedron too, but there isn't enough room left.<br /><br />I'm invested now, but I wish I wasn't.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15658191215036345242" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1642228558" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1642228558" />
    <a title="malayna" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/55992181-malayna"><img alt="malayna" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1592140082p2/55992181.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1642228558?book_show_action=true">May 18, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="malayna" class="user" itemprop="url" name="malayna" href="/user/show/55992181-malayna">malayna</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/55992181-malayna?shelf=5-stars">5-stars</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1642228558" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8559392423707592660">THERE WAS A MISTAKE IN MY PREVIOUS REVIEW***<br/><br/>MY OPINION: *****<br/><br/>I sincerely love this series, no matter how middle-grade it is.<br/><br/>WHAT this book only has 470 reviews?? We need to advertise this book a LOT! It's seriously amazing and something every kid should read sometime in their lifetime.<br/><br/>It's not that it's deep or personal or has a really strong message. It's just a really good book with lots of plot twists, adventure, friendship, and growing up. <br/><br/>ANYWAYS, on with the review!<br/><br/>SO I have read this book</span>
  <span id="freeText8559392423707592660" style="display:none">THERE WAS A MISTAKE IN MY PREVIOUS REVIEW***<br /><br />MY OPINION: *****<br /><br />I sincerely love this series, no matter how middle-grade it is.<br /><br />WHAT this book only has 470 reviews?? We need to advertise this book a LOT! It's seriously amazing and something every kid should read sometime in their lifetime.<br /><br />It's not that it's deep or personal or has a really strong message. It's just a really good book with lots of plot twists, adventure, friendship, and growing up. <br /><br />ANYWAYS, on with the review!<br /><br />SO I have read this book about two years ago, as well as last year, and this year I'm reading it again! I'm sure that next year will be another time to read the series as BOOK SEVEN will be coming out around this time!<br /><br />If you guys HAVE NOT read my most recent reviews of the first two books, then this will be news to you. If you HAVE read my most recent reviews (aww thanks you guys are amazing) then go ahead and skip ahead to the final count. ANYWAYS, I have been tracking the number of Sophitz, Sokeefe, and Sodex moments, though I do plan to add other ships should I find any evidence. The final tally after this book is:<br /><br />Sophitz: 23<br />Sokeefe: 10<br />Sodex: 15<br /><br />AS WE CAN SEE, SOPHITZ IS STILL WINNING BY A LOT :D :D :D <br /><br />#sophitzshipperinthemidst<br /><br />ANYWAYS, there WERE a lot more Sokeefe tags in this book :\ I'll let you guys stew on that.<br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[AND for those of you who have read <i>Nightfall</i> already, PLEASE note that Sodex died. It sunk. I'm sorry Sodex shippers. AND NO I have not read the book but I LOVE spoilers and I have heard quite a few... <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />Let's talk about the characters.<br /><br />I always find these reviews the most fun because it's easy to find things to talk about. Huh... maybe I do like middle-grade better than I thought.<br /><br />Sophie. I do enjoy reading from her point of view, though I would appreciate if it was MULTI-PERSPECTIVE (how cool would that be, reading from Fitz or Keefe's POV??!) though Sophie IS kind of hilarious. Her thoughts are rambling (like mine) and I find that she is very perceptive. She's also determined, brave, courageous, loyal, worrisome, and kind. She always wants to protect her friends and family above all else, even if means breaking the law or doing the wrong thing to do so.<br /><br />Fitz. I loved him so much (as usual). I loved him EVEN more this book than the first book, because HE WASN'T a total JERK this time around, seeing as Sophie hadn't done anything (well... not that much) wrong. Fitz is so sweet and he's also a great friend, though he's kind of oblivious and sometimes gives a girl false hopes (including me) THOUGH MAYBE IT IS INTENTIONAL AND HE LIKES SOPHIE?! Hmm... gotta stew more on that one.<br /><br />Keefe. I loved Keefe though I DO NOT SHIP HIM WITH SOPHIE, only because he's too... lighthearted, if that makes any sense. I LOVE the positivity but Sophie needs to be with more of a serious guy, the one who's going to listen to her and not try to crack a joke. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I DO KNOW that he gets a LOT more serious in the upcoming books, but still... <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> Keefe was hilarious, as usual, and his lightening the mood action really did help a lot of the time. But still... not the guy for Sophie, if ya know what I mean.<br /><br />Dex. All my life, I've harbored a secret... dislike of Dex. Is that just me? I mean, he's a great friend and all but honestly, he's WAY too desparate and obvious (please don't hate me now). <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[And his wanting to prove himself really annoyed me because why make a weapon for a reputation when you have your friends to think about? <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> Dex DOES do some really cute things (Iggy, the ring, etc).<br /><br />Biana was just the same as usual. I always forget that Biana isn't as close to Sophie yet, though it's definitely getting warmer, seeing as she's part of the team. But we cannot forget their rocky beginning. And the initiation of their friendship. Though Biana WOULD be perfect with Keefe AT SOME POINTS: they're both happy and willing to think about things in an optimistic sense while the others think about things in a literal sense.<br /><br />BTW for those of you who were asking, here are my SHIPS! (ONLY READ IF YOU HAVE READ NEVERSEEN AND ABOVE--THERE ARE SOME DIFFERENT CHARACTERS)<br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[<br />SophieXFitz=Sophitz (obvs)<br />BianaXTam=Bam?<br />KeefeXLinh=Kinh??<br />TamXMarella=Tarella?<br /><br />IF THOSE DO NOT WORK OUT (WHICH I AM SURE A LOT OF THEM WILL NOT, HERE IS MY OTHER VERSION THAT I AM SURE A LOT OF SOPHITZ SHIPPERS WILL HATE ME FOR)<br /><br />SophieXKeefe=Sokeefe (though I do not REALLY like this ship but she cannot be with Tam so that leaves me no choice)<br />FitzXLinh=Finh (please don't hate me, it's kinda cute)<br />DexXMarella=Darella? (eh, I don't really think about Dex that much and neither do I think about Marella so why not)<br />TamXBiana=Bam (I STILL LOVE THIS SHIP)<br /><br /> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />SO yeah, that about wraps it up! I would recommend this book to kids who are looking for a long adventurous novel that is age-appropriate and genuinely funny.<br /><br />Main Character: Sophie<br />Sidekick(s): Fitz, Dex, Biana, Keefe, etc<br />Villain(s): Neverseen, Stina, Council, etc<br />Fantasy Elements: This book has fanatic creatures, settings, characters, etc</span>
  <a data-text-id="8559392423707592660" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_796313509" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/796313509" />
    <a title="Christina Anastasia Stavridi" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14155400-christina-anastasia-stavridi"><img alt="Christina Anastasia Stavridi" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer796313509" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6406108825763689616">After almost a year of waiting I finally got to read the third book in the keeper of the lost cities series (which, turns out, its not a trilogy so this is no the end keeper fans). We’re sucked into the story from page one and unlike the previous books it lead somewhere. Don’t get me wrong I liked 1 & 2( I am a keeper fan), but while all the journey is important in the end it didn’t lead somewhere.<br/><br/>I do believe Everblaze was different from 1 & 2, things start to get more serious and dangerous and</span>
  <span id="freeText6406108825763689616" style="display:none">After almost a year of waiting I finally got to read the third book in the keeper of the lost cities series (which, turns out, its not a trilogy so this is no the end keeper fans). We’re sucked into the story from page one and unlike the previous books it lead somewhere. Don’t get me wrong I liked 1 &amp; 2( I am a keeper fan), but while all the journey is important in the end it didn’t lead somewhere.<br /><br />I do believe Everblaze was different from 1 &amp; 2, things start to get more serious and dangerous and while it still clearly is a MG book I think kids above that age range will find it interesting. (I say more because I already do). <br /><br />All the characters we know return once again and it becomes clear they ALL play a role in the bigger picture. Even those we thought didn’t really matter. My personal favorite is, was and will be keefe. I’m happy to say we see quite a lot of him (good enough reason to read Everblaze, never mind everything else). Since we follow Sophie when it comes to keefe we read conversations he has with her and they’re still mostly funny and cute with teasing remarks.<br /><br />Everblaze it’s not a light book which you can freely take breaks from. It’s a book you read without many interruptions in a quite room on a comfortable sofa. <br /><br />In books 1 and 2 I have to say the times Sophie s’ abilities were mentioned and complimented or Sophie herself are so many, it’s annoying. I had to roll my eyes too many times while reading it. In Everblaze we’re still reminded of her powers but not at the same level. It makes us enjoy the story without thinking ‘yeah, okay, you said that already there are more important things you should be focusing on and there are more characters’. <br /><br />Another thing I liked was the relationships. NO, not the romance. I’m not much for romance. I meant Sophie’s relationship with her adoptive parents, her friends and the rest of the characters. The triangle or quadrangle? it’s still in the background but true friendship exists between the five friends and it’s above anything teenage hormones can do. <br /><br />Everblaze is on my ‘favorites’ list (though, granted, many books are) and a big part of that is the storyline. Things got so much more interesting and I couldn’t wait to find out what happened after the parts I’d read. Loved every page of it, Messenger deserves congrats for creating it.<br /><br />---------<br /><br />And we have a title!Awesome can't wait to read this.I need to know what's going to happen. Everblaze huh?I should have seen it coming.I guess its pretty appropriate and it's a cool title.I actually like it better than the other books titles.<br />Also I need to read it but i don't want it to end!<br /><br /><br />EDIT--<br /><br />The COVER...THE COVER!!!!!It's FITZ...FITZ! Finally! ***squeals happily**<br />Excuse me while I fangirl. <br /><br />Okay,now.They are falling from a building.Hmm...Wonder why that is.Ughh.Once again I need to know what happens. I mean,come on why are they falling from a building? And are those crystals?<br /><br />And now excuse me I'm going to stare the beautiful cover once again.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6406108825763689616" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16071454-matilda?shelf=loved-books">loved-books</a>,

<span id="freeTextContainer12690439450799153998"><b> Stop what you are doing- now </b><br/><br/>Go read this series. Ok, that’s all I want. It’s one of the series that I stare at how many Goodreads rating it gets and cry slightly. The ratings are high- because this book and previous two are amazing but like no one has read it.<br/><br/>For me to sum this up for you: It’s like reading harry potter again and Percy Jackson, that feeling for the first time when you start reading it and fall into that world with the characters and the world building. <b> That is what it is like</b></span>
  <span id="freeText12690439450799153998" style="display:none"><b> Stop what you are doing- now </b><br /><br />Go read this series. Ok, that’s all I want. It’s one of the series that I stare at how many Goodreads rating it gets and cry slightly. The ratings are high- because this book and previous two are amazing but like no one has read it.<br /><br />For me to sum this up for you: It’s like reading harry potter again and Percy Jackson, that feeling for the first time when you start reading it and fall into that world with the characters and the world building. <b> That is what it is like to read this series </b><br /><br />It is in no way a Harry Potter or Percy Jackson rip off, it is nothing like them apart from it pulls you in and you will fall in love with the world and characters- and you want to be part of it.<br /><b> I cannot stress enough how amazing this series is </b><br /><br /><br />The third book just takes things higher- I need the next book now, like now.</span>

<div id="review_1253071952" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1253071952" />
    <a title="Christina (A Reader of Fictions)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2602702-christina-a-reader-of-fictions"><img alt="Christina (A Reader of Fictions)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1464118116p2/2602702.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1253071952?book_show_action=true">Apr 12, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Christina (A Reader of Fictions)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Christina (A Reader of Fictions)" href="/user/show/2602702-christina-a-reader-of-fictions">Christina (A Reader of Fictions)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1253071952" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18385333647725897558">Wow, I can’t believe I’m doing this, but I have to give Everblaze three stars. The series is still ridiculous to the max, but the characterization and plotting are worlds better than they were in book one.<br/><br/>The reason this series has been steadily improving can be summed up in one word: Keefe. He is slowly taking over this series by sheer force of personality. He’s even, even more slowly, helping Sophie to loosen up a bit, which she sorely needs. Keefe has character development like whoa in this, </span>
  <span id="freeText18385333647725897558" style="display:none">Wow, I can’t believe I’m doing this, but I have to give Everblaze three stars. The series is still ridiculous to the max, but the characterization and plotting are worlds better than they were in book one.<br /><br />The reason this series has been steadily improving can be summed up in one word: Keefe. He is slowly taking over this series by sheer force of personality. He’s even, even more slowly, helping Sophie to loosen up a bit, which she sorely needs. Keefe has character development like whoa in this, and he does it all with his characteristic snark, banter, and warmth. He is the BEST. Any scene with him in it was compelling and engaging.<br /><br />Unlike the prior novels in the series, Everblaze wasn’t so much of a slog. Bring on book four, so long as it has oodles and oodles of the Keefester.</span>

          </span>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('ty3MPxOpgp9vUSdkL0YBWZF4x7/nWN1w5IZjsxsiri5Www2wLxNh+7x47M+EdFZkigbLC7mLyoHby8tbuZQd+g==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('nw3dfVj6mmMZg40nHm9M4d6ypyhtGxSasdrrbI8ACqN+4xzyZEB5B8qqRoy1XRvcxcyrnDPIA2uOl0OELba5dw==')})
  }
//]]>
